Because insects possess identifiable common characteristics, they can be recognised as a distinct biological group and assigned a taxonomic rank.\n\nSimilarly, many other groups of organisms can be recognised based on shared characteristics.\n\nIt is important to remember that:\n\nA group represents a category.\nA category denotes a rank.\nEvery rank (taxon) represents a unit of classification.\nTaxonomic groups are distinct biological entities, not merely collections of organisms having similar external appearance (morphological aggregates).\nTaxonomic Hierarchy\n\nTaxonomical studies of all known organisms have led to the development of universally accepted taxonomic categories.\n\nThese categories are:\n\nKingdom\nPhylum (Division in plants)\nClass\nOrder\nFamily\nGenus\nSpecies\n\nAmong all these categories, Species is the lowest taxonomic category.\n\nThe placement of an organism into different categories depends primarily on the knowledge of its characteristics. Studying these characteristics helps identify:\n\nSimilarities among organisms of the same kind.\nDifferences between organisms belonging to different groups.",
